    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer4471363464833490626">In his work as a Miami crime scene investigator, Dexter Morgan is accustomed to seeing evil deeds...particulary because, on occasion, he rather enjoys committing them himself. Guided by his dark Passenger - the voice inside him that helps stalk his prey - he lives his outwardly normal life adhering to one simple rule: he only kills very bad people.<br/><br/>Dexter slides through lif</span>
  <span id="freeText4471363464833490626" style="display:none">In his work as a Miami crime scene investigator, Dexter Morgan is accustomed to seeing evil deeds...particulary because, on occasion, he rather enjoys committing them himself. Guided by his dark Passenger - the voice inside him that helps stalk his prey - he lives his outwardly normal life adhering to one simple rule: he only kills very bad people.<br /><br />Dexter slides through life undetected, working as a blood splatter analyst for the Miami Police Department, helping his fiancee raise her two adorable (if somewhat...unique) children, and always planning his next jaunt as Dexter the Dark Avenger under the light of the full moon.<br /><br />But everthing changes when Dexter is called to a gruesome double homicide. Dex realizes he's dealing with someone a whole lot more sinister than he is and it sends the Dark Passenger into hiding. And when something scares your friendly neighborhood serial killer, you know it's serious...<br /><br />More used to inspiring fear then experiencing it, Dex must investigate, while simultaneously coping with his demanding family. If he's to save himself, and those around him, Dexter must pose questions he's never dared ask - where does evil come from, and does it hide inside everyone...?</span>
  <a data-text-id="4471363464833490626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_519209127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/519209127" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/519209127?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519209127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14940228040707092123"><i>Far above the aimless scurrying of the city<b> IT</b> watched, and<b> IT</b> waited. There was plenty to see, as always, and <b>IT</b> was in no hurry. <b>IT</b> had done this many time before, and would do so again, endlessly and forever. That was what <b>IT</b> was for. Right now there were so many different choices to consider, and no reason to do anything but consider them until the right one was clear. And then <b>IT</b> would start again, gather the faithful, give them their bright miracle, and <b>IT</b> would feel once more the wonder a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14940228040707092123" style="display:none"><i>Far above the aimless scurrying of the city<b> IT</b> watched, and<b> IT</b> waited. There was plenty to see, as always, and <b>IT</b> was in no hurry. <b>IT</b> had done this many time before, and would do so again, endlessly and forever. That was what <b>IT</b> was for. Right now there were so many different choices to consider, and no reason to do anything but consider them until the right one was clear. And then <b>IT</b> would start again, gather the faithful, give them their bright miracle, and <b>IT</b> would feel once more the wonder and joy and swelling rightness of their pain.<br>All that would come again. It was just a matter of waiting for the right moment.<br>And <b>IT</b> had all the time in the world.</i><br><br><a href="https://s1183.beta.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Dexter_zpsee92f103.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547668442i/26927409.jpg" alt=" photo Dexter_zpsee92f103.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Michael C. Hall plays Dexter</b><br><br>Jeff Lindsay really put a lot of noses out of joint with this one. He has fans of the show and fans of the previous two books to please and this one just hit a jarring note with a lot of people. <br><br>It is similar to being strapped to a board with duct tape and you open your eyes to find there is a menacing serial killer standing over you with a bloody scalpel. You make the connection that it is your blood on that scalpel. <br><br>You pass out. <br><br>You come back to consciousness when he starts slicing and dicing...oh so lovingly...your inner thigh. <br><br>You scream. <br><br>You negotiate. <br><br>He laughs, soaking up your terror like an extra large roll of Downy paper towels, and then before he really starts going to work on removing some appendages or organs he just lets you go. You feel relief as you stumble down the middle of a four lane road in Miami dripping blood hoping someone will stop before you become a hood ornament on a Kenworth supercab. Then you get mad thinking isn’t my body good enough for even a damn serial killer. What the f**k is wrong with me? Didn’t I scream loud enough? Didn’t my blood spurt as well as the next guy? <br><br>You feel oddly let down.<br><br>The interesting aspect of Dexter Morgan’s character is that he is a regular run of the mill serial killer with a code of ethics that was instilled in him by his cop stepfather Harry. Now those codes that have been instilled in young Dexter are also the same codes that keep average people like me or you from being strapped to a board feeling Dexter joyfully dismembering the fine temple we’ve spent so much time sculpting. In this third installment Lindsay chose to instill a supernatural element to the life and times of Dexter Morgan. Readers were upset, with feelings ranging from betrayal to outrage. They don’t want to believe that something netherworld evil might be controlling Dexter. They want to believe that Dexter is just well Dexter, a really nasty serial killer that has a code that allows us all to feel reassured that he is only killing really bad people, so it isn’t sick and disgusting that we are rooting for him.<br><br><a href="https://s1183.beta.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/DexterintheDark_zpsd41ff767.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547668442i/26927410._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo DexterintheDark_zpsd41ff767.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>I was fortunate enough to have Jeff Lindsay sign my run of Dexter books.</b><br><br>Well Dexter has a shadow that he calls the <b>DARK PASSENGER</b>. For the first time in his life this constant companion, this trusted advisor, disappears leaving him feeling empty like a body without a soul. He is having disturbing dreams for the first time in his life. <br><br><i>”No, this was my subconscious. If it was crying out in pain at the threat of abandonment, I knew exactly what it feared losing: the Dark Passenger. My bosom buddy, my constant companion on my journey through life’s sorrows and sharp pleasures. That was the fear behind the dream: losing the thing that had been so very much a part of me, and actually defined me, for my whole life.”</i><br><br>In the midst of a new case with bodies burned and their heads lopped off and replaced with ceramic bull heads Dexter encounters something dark and dangerous, something so creepy that the Dark Passenger scurries away leaving Dexter feeling exposed and weak and very human. <br><br><i>”Dashing Dexter does not know the meaning of fear. That would have to mean that the roaring thump of my heart, the parching of my mouth, and the sweat pouring out of my hands was no more than massive uneasiness. <br>I did not enjoy the feeling. I was no longer the Knight of the Knife. My blade and my armor were in some subbasement of the castle, and I was on the field of battle without them, a suddenly soft and tasty victim, and for no reason I could name I was sure that something had my scent in its ravening nostrils.”</i><br><br><a href="https://s1183.beta.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/912a7aa2-56da-4dc1-826c-87d39bcafeb5_zps11e1e908.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547668442i/26927411._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 912a7aa2-56da-4dc1-826c-87d39bcafeb5_zps11e1e908.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>King Solomon killed his brother because he had something DARK inside him.</b><br><br>Dexter is also in the middle of wedding plans, all part of his overall scheme to appear normal. The children of his bride, Cody and Astor are far from normal kids. In fact they too have shadows that drive them to want to inflict pain. He feels pressured to teach them the code of Harry, but like all kids they are impatient to skip the work and get to the fun. Dexter, without the reassuring presence of his Dark Passenger feels his life unraveling. He becomes the main focus of something known as IT, something that was around in the days of Solomon, something so powerful so fear inspiring that Dexter finds himself being controlled and helpless to escape. <br><br>Hopefully in the fourth Dexter Morgan book Lindsay will choose to get back to the regular “mortal” adventures of our favorite serial killer. I was not as bothered by the supernatural elements as much as other readers were because I feel that any perception made by a human being can seem supernatural. The whole idea of Voodoo is that it only works if people believe that it can. I think the same idea can be applied to the cult of Moloch that wrecks so much havoc on poor Dexter in this novel. <br><br><a href="https://s1183.beta.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Moloch_zps403a3be4.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547668442i/26927412._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo Moloch_zps403a3be4.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>The Cult of Moloch or MLK.</b><br><br>I’ll end this review with a bit of Florida environmental commentary that Lindsay slips into the novel. <br><br><i>”The island we headed for was one of the smaller ones. Half of a forty-foot sports fisherman lay on the beach at a crazy angle, and the pine trees inland of the beach were hung with chunks of Styrofoam, tattered cloth, and wispy shreds of plastic sheeting and garbage bags. Other than that, it was just the way the Native Americans had left it, a peaceful little chunk of land covered with Australian pines, condoms, and beer cans.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14940228040707092123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6028440" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6028440" />
    <a title="Sean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/138600-sean"><img alt="Sean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562511132p2/138600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6028440?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean" href="/user/show/138600-sean">Sean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6028440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2572653855102258976">Disappointingly mystical. In attempting to "explain" Dexter, Lindsay has robbed him of much of his appeal. Anne Rice tried this in Queen of the Damned, to much the same effect: Dexter's unique talents, like Lestat's, were better left a mystery.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1223582568" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223582568" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223582568?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/23279899-dexter-in-the-dark">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Thriller and serial killer fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Edward by: </span>
      John
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223582568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12278266303849614505">Day three of my Dexter Morgan marathon, and Book Three is done. I might actually do this Seven Books in Seven Days Challenge. Yay me. *cue crickets and awkward glances*<br/><br/>I think I'm in the minority when I say that I liked this one very much, but I know why most readers (or, if you prefer, fans of this series) did not like it. People enjoy their comfort zones. <i>Dexter in the Dark</i> takes fans of the series out an established realistic environ by alluding to a possible supernatural origin to the Dark P</span>
  <span id="freeText12278266303849614505" style="display:none">Day three of my Dexter Morgan marathon, and Book Three is done. I might actually do this Seven Books in Seven Days Challenge. Yay me. *cue crickets and awkward glances*<br /><br />I think I'm in the minority when I say that I liked this one very much, but I know why most readers (or, if you prefer, fans of this series) did not like it. People enjoy their comfort zones. <i>Dexter in the Dark</i> takes fans of the series out an established realistic environ by alluding to a possible supernatural origin to the Dark Passenger. I mean, how dare Lindsay suddenly want to do something different mid-series? The sheer audacity of a move like that! Imagine if Alex Cross suddenly found himself up against demons, and Columbo began slaying werewolves with a cast of his lazy eye. Ludicrous! <br /><br />(Oh, lookey there, I spelled "ludicrous" right this time! Take that, Ludacris!)<br /><br />I understand you have to follow certain rules when you take on a series. But I also know how soul crushing repetition can be. Nothing dampens a fiery imagination like a bucket full of monotony. Lindsay tried something new, and fans balked. Yet, in my opinion, he was vaguely successful in branching out. I dug the concept. I don't think I would have went full on evil-older-than-man to explain Dexter's inner bad boy, but it is what it is. I give him an A for effort.<br /><br />Once again, because I listened to this one, we have a split decision on our hands. Three stars for the story, and five for the performance. So, you guessed it, four stars.<br /><br />In summation: Lindsay swings for the fences and connects. Some fans see this book as a foul ball, but I prefer to think of it as an on-base. It's definitely not a home run, and I have no idea where these fucking baseball metaphors are coming from. I hate baseball. Goddamn it...<br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: Cody ex Machina.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12278266303849614505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_63150963" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63150963" />
    <a title="Lightreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads"><img alt="Lightreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230606449p2/1836077.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63150963?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lightreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lightreads" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads">Lightreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63150963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7762308776307413067">Adventures of a sociopathic serial killer who generally only cuts up people who hurt children.<br/><br/>Okay, awesome. Lindsay has clearly done his research – the way Dexter completely fails to get sex, his inflated perceptions of his own intelligence, his completely oblivious sexism, his utter lack of the empathic reflex, it's all <i>perfect</i>. People who know me were shocked I hadn't read these books before. Mostly it was that I knew what they were about, and I thought it would be stupid because I didn't bel</span>
  <span id="freeText7762308776307413067" style="display:none">Adventures of a sociopathic serial killer who generally only cuts up people who hurt children.<br /><br />Okay, awesome. Lindsay has clearly done his research – the way Dexter completely fails to get sex, his inflated perceptions of his own intelligence, his completely oblivious sexism, his utter lack of the empathic reflex, it's all <i>perfect</i>. People who know me were shocked I hadn't read these books before. Mostly it was that I knew what they were about, and I thought it would be stupid because I didn't believe a sociopath with that kind of organized offender behavior would ever follow a set of rules on who he could and couldn't kill. But actually that's part of Dexter's fetish – the stalking, the perfect planning, being neat and clean and sure. And who knew these books would be so flipping funny?<br /><br />Unfortunately, the third book wanders straight off into lala land. I mean, seriously, the hell was that? Lindsay pretty much ruined all the interesting work he'd done on the damage and disfunctions that lead to sociopathy by going for . . . what, demons? It would have been fine as a slide into psychopathic delusion, or even as Dexter's personal metaphor to explain what he is and why. But no. Demons! *helpless hand gestures* <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7762308776307413067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review63150963">

<div id="review_689398737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689398737" />
    <a title="Thomas Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6949571-thomas-paul"><img alt="Thomas Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396448679p2/6949571.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/689398737?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Paul" href="/user/show/6949571-thomas-paul">Thomas Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689398737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3884878494106059670">It's sad to see such a good series descend to this level. This book was a real disappointment. It's hard to know where to start but the overall premise of the book, that Dexter's "Dark Passenger" is actually a supernatural possession by some kind of child of Moloch an eternal something-or-other, lacks so much believability that it ruins the entire series. What made the first two books so good was that Dexter was the sociopath trying to live in the real world. His "Dark Passenger" was simply a di</span>
  <span id="freeText3884878494106059670" style="display:none">It's sad to see such a good series descend to this level. This book was a real disappointment. It's hard to know where to start but the overall premise of the book, that Dexter's "Dark Passenger" is actually a supernatural possession by some kind of child of Moloch an eternal something-or-other, lacks so much believability that it ruins the entire series. What made the first two books so good was that Dexter was the sociopath trying to live in the real world. His "Dark Passenger" was simply a different part of Dexter's personality. The success of the books was that we rooted for Dexter and his "Dark Passenger" in spite of him being a sociopath. But how can we root for some horrible monster that possesses Dexter and forces him to kill?<br /><br />But Lindsay goes too far even with his idea of how someone becomes a sociopath. Every child, at least according to Lindsay, who is abused as a child, grows up to be a serial killer. Rita's two kids both become sociopaths because they were abused by their father. But that isn't how it happens in the real world. Not all serial killers were abused and not everyone who is abused becomes a serial killer. We can root for Dexter when he is unique and only killing other serial killers, but how can we root for him to create more serial killers? Dexter should be sending the children for intense psychotherapy, not lessons in how to kill.<br /><br />And worst of all, the book is simply boring. Nothing much happens. There are murders but it is impossible to keep straight who is killing who and the murders (and murderers) are almost irrelevant. We hear more about donuts and wedding caterers than we do about anything else. And there really is no mystery in the story. We find out in the first pages of the book who did it although I kept hoping that the book wasn't really going to be this stupid and that Lindsay would give us some other surprise solution. I am fairly confident that this is the last Dexter book I will be reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3884878494106059670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2986588" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2986588" />
    <a title="Brooke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/126262-brooke"><img alt="Brooke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448065679p2/126262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2986588?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooke" href="/user/show/126262-brooke">Brooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126262-brooke?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126262-brooke?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2986588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17687017321694871515">If book-Dexter was running along a slightly different track than TV-Dexter before this, Dexter in the Dark takes as far away as it can possibly get. <br/><br/>TV-Dexter is grounded squarely in reality. A very bloody reality, but reality nonetheless. The first two books in the series hinted a bit at a supernatural element; the first book's dreams, for example, and they way our beloved serial killer referred to his dark side as a separate persona who resided in him. I always figured this was metaphorical, b</span>
  <span id="freeText17687017321694871515" style="display:none">If book-Dexter was running along a slightly different track than TV-Dexter before this, Dexter in the Dark takes as far away as it can possibly get. <br /><br />TV-Dexter is grounded squarely in reality. A very bloody reality, but reality nonetheless. The first two books in the series hinted a bit at a supernatural element; the first book's dreams, for example, and they way our beloved serial killer referred to his dark side as a separate persona who resided in him. I always figured this was metaphorical, but book 3 makes it clear that this is quite literal. Dexter's Dark Passenger leaves him after being scared off by a darker force that is killing people in Miami. Dexter is left without his murderous intuition, without his bloodthirst, and without his emotionless demeanor. <br /><br />Now, I've seen a lot of reviews that simply hated this. I was prepared to hate it. I didn't though, for a few reasons. For one, it goes a long way in explaining the dreams from book 1, something I never really bought. If Dexter has this supernatural force living in him, then I can reasonably believe that he'd be receptive to dreams about things that he couldn't know. Secondly, I'm sort of glad to have two very distinct Dexter universes to enjoy. If the show and the books mirrored each other too much, it would start to get boring. Third, it was a serial killer "creation story" that I haven't really encountered before. I'm not jumping up and down over it, but I'm willing to give this idea a try.<br /><br />Other than the plot, I once again enjoyed the dark humor and Dexter's internal voice. I really wish we'd get more scenes between Dexter and Deborah; since book-Deborah knows about her brother's dark side, it just seems like it's a situation ripe for mining (I just reread my review of the last book, and I see I had used the word 'ripe' then, too. Clearly I A) feel very strongly about this, and B) need a larger vocabulary). I want to see more conversations and interaction between them regarding Dexter's hobby. I feel like Jeff Lindsay has missed an opportunity twice now to really deliver on this. Otherwise, Dexter's getting 4 stars from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17687017321694871515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2190384597" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2190384597" />
    <a title="Vivian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian"><img alt="Vivian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458107851p2/3947172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2190384597?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=2017-odyssey">2017-odyssey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2190384597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5453386536237386829">I really should have liked this more. <br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>I stood up. It was all too much. I could not even meet my own expectations, and to be asked to deal with all theirs was too suffocating.</blockquote>
</b> <br/><br/>Dexter's growth during this book is good, a solid advancement of his character rather than just rinse and repeat that afflicts so many series. The majority of it is driven by external forces, Dexter's interaction with other characters, but in this episode the Dark Passenger takes center stage. <br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>I closed my eyes and li</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText5453386536237386829" style="display:none">I really should have liked this more. <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>I stood up. It was all too much. I could not even meet my own expectations, and to be asked to deal with all theirs was too suffocating.</blockquote>
</b> <br /><br />Dexter's growth during this book is good, a solid advancement of his character rather than just rinse and repeat that afflicts so many series. The majority of it is driven by external forces, Dexter's interaction with other characters, but in this episode the Dark Passenger takes center stage. <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>I closed my eyes and listened to the novel emotions gurgling through me. Feeling--what authentic human fun. Next, I could join a bowling league.</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />Dexter's relationship with Rita is advancing rapidly and her children, Astor and Cody are looking forward to their new father.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>And even worse, I could tell that somehow it had become my problem; the children expected me to bail them out, and Rita was clearly prepared to lock and load and open fire on me. </blockquote>
</b><br /><br />The thing that did not work for me was the heavy-handed omniscient viewpoint. I found it too fantastical and a clumsy attempt at explaining the Dark Passenger and the story would have been fine without it. It was dissatisfying.<br /><br />Words to live by:<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>"No, it's not fair," I said. "Nothing in life is fair. Fair is a dirty word and I'll thank you not to use that language around me."</blockquote>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5453386536237386829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15429441874026060573">I very much enjoyed part three in the Dexter series. Compared to the preceding book, this was a lot heavier on the humor and in the case of Dexter I really think this is to prefer. In part two, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/136081.Dearly_Devoted_Dexter__Dexter___2_' title='Dearly Devoted Dexter (Dexter, #2) by Jeff Lindsay' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dearly Devoted Dexter</a>, Lindsay tried his damnedest to shock and gross us out - and he was quite successful.   <span id="freeText15429441874026060573" style="display:none">I very much enjoyed part three in the Dexter series. Compared to the preceding book, this was a lot heavier on the humor and in the case of Dexter I really think this is to prefer. In part two, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/136081.Dearly_Devoted_Dexter__Dexter___2_" title="Dearly Devoted Dexter (Dexter, #2) by Jeff Lindsay" rel="nofollow noopener">Dearly Devoted Dexter</a>, Lindsay tried his damnedest to shock and gross us out - and he was quite successful. And that's the reason for the missing star. Still, a really good read. </span>

<div id="review_141993462" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141993462" />
    <a title="Aaron Geno" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4781870-aaron-geno"><img alt="Aaron Geno" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307718324p2/4781870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141993462?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Geno" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Geno" href="/user/show/4781870-aaron-geno">Aaron Geno</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fair-minded fans of the first two books.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4781870-aaron-geno?shelf=1990-to-present">1990-to-present</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4781870-aaron-geno?shelf=dark-thriller-mystery">dark-thriller-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141993462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7904167806676106282">There's a lot of dislike for this book going on in these reviews. It's totally unjustified.<br/>First, this may come as news to some people, but Dexter the show is not Dexter the [Author: Jeff Lindsay] series. The books are darker (if you're a fan of the show, 1. Yes, it's possible, and 2. Don't pick up the series here; start with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17231.Darkly_Dreaming_Dexter__Dexter___1_' title='Darkly Dreaming Dexter (Dexter, #1) by Jeff Lindsay' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkly Dreaming Dexter</a>). And yes, there's a supernatural element to this book. The thing is, it's not new. I would argue that the supernatural element is present even in th</span>
  <span id="freeText7904167806676106282" style="display:none">There's a lot of dislike for this book going on in these reviews. It's totally unjustified.<br />First, this may come as news to some people, but Dexter the show is not Dexter the [Author: Jeff Lindsay] series. The books are darker (if you're a fan of the show, 1. Yes, it's possible, and 2. Don't pick up the series here; start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17231.Darkly_Dreaming_Dexter__Dexter___1_" title="Darkly Dreaming Dexter (Dexter, #1) by Jeff Lindsay" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkly Dreaming Dexter</a>). And yes, there's a supernatural element to this book. The thing is, it's not new. I would argue that the supernatural element is present even in the show, if dialed down, but the books certainly have never left ambiguity concerning the shadows and Dexter's Passenger. When Dexter speaks about his Passenger, he's not waxing philosophical or speaking metaphorically. If you read books 1 and 2 and are still willing to gripe about the supernatural in this book, there's no talking to you.<br /><br />This, to me, is the best of the series so far (I have yet to read 4 and 5); there was very little of the novel during which I didn't have a sense of dread, and it was with great pains that I made myself stop 70-odd pages from the end (Nook version) on day one so that I could go to sleep. If you've enjoyed the books so far, take a chance on this one, too. I suspect most readers giving it a fair shake won't be disappointed. Even Lindsay's slammed-into-a-brick-wall-abrupt endings are losing their grating quality for me.<br /><br /><b>*****SPOILERS BELOW*****</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I mention that the books are darker. They are. If you read books one and two, you know that Astor and Cody both were far more traumatized by Rita's ex-husband's abuse than the TV version. Cody is explicitly referred to as having his own shadow (akin to Dexter's Passenger). And yes, he kills someone in the book, though it's not under nefarious circumstances (at least not of his making). I feel that the kids' needs for guidance make them more relevant to the story and to Dexter than in the TV show, but opinions will vary. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_173505727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173505727" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5552109-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405580498p2/5552109.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173505727?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/5552109-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/11270473-dexter-in-the-dark">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">twisted souls</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173505727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8017884418338628239"><b>Book Info</b>: <u>Genre</u>: Supernatural Thriller/Police Procedural<br/><u>Reading Level</u>: Adult<br/><u>Recommended for</u>: twisted people<br/><u>Trigger Warnings</u>: murder, human sacrifice<br/><br/><b>My Thoughts</b>: So, again, this is my second time through this book. I originally picked it up in 2010 and read it shortly thereafter, so it's been around three years since I first read these books.<br/><br/>This book has a lot more of the dark humor that we so love with Dexter, superimposing the comedic wedding plans and Dexter's attempts to work with Astor and</span>
  <span id="freeText8017884418338628239" style="display:none"><b>Book Info</b>: <u>Genre</u>: Supernatural Thriller/Police Procedural<br /><u>Reading Level</u>: Adult<br /><u>Recommended for</u>: twisted people<br /><u>Trigger Warnings</u>: murder, human sacrifice<br /><br /><b>My Thoughts</b>: So, again, this is my second time through this book. I originally picked it up in 2010 and read it shortly thereafter, so it's been around three years since I first read these books.<br /><br />This book has a lot more of the dark humor that we so love with Dexter, superimposing the comedic wedding plans and Dexter's attempts to work with Astor and Cody with the dangerous killings (and danger to Dexter himself) in a very effective way. I was particularly amused by the description of Dexter and Deborah's visit to a New Age shop: <blockquote>“<i>We stepped in..A suffocating cloud of sickly sweet incense rolled over me, and I could tell that my inner enhancement had begun with a complete overhaul of my lungs. Through the smoke I could dimly see a large yellow silk banner hung along one wall that stated WE ARE ALL ONE. It did not say one of what. A recording played softly, the sound of someone who seemed to be fighting off an overdose of downers by occasionally ringing a series of small bells. A waterfall murmured in the background and I am sure that my spirit would have soared, if only I had one. Since I didn't, I found the whole thing just a bit irritating.</i>”</blockquote> I also frequently laughed at Dexter's impatience with Cody and Astor's impatience to begin learning the Dark Path.<br /><br />The hints of the supernatural made in the first books are now fully formed and in motion, thus I have changed my genre designation. I really enjoyed the prologue, and the bits intertwined in the story, that give us some more details on the Dark Passenger and its history. Although I really like reading the books from Dexter's point-of-view (even when he is speaking of himself in the third person), I also liked that we had a hint of the Watcher's thoughts throughout the book, too. I think it really increased the tension, letting us know that Dexter really <i>was</i> in danger (oh NOES) and it certainly kept me on my toes. As Dexter put it, “<i>Feeling—what authentic human fun. Next I would join a bowling league. Find a chat room online and talk about New Age self-help and alternative herbal medicine for hemorrhoids. Welcome to the human race, Dexter, the endlessly futile and pointless human race.</i>”<br /><br />I was very surprised that Dexter had never heard of the stories about Solomon and demons, or about Moloch, honestly. Or maybe he had heard the stories but never knew the background, I'm not sure, but I immediately was aware of the background. Scary stuff. But wonderful. I really do enjoy these books. I hope you will, too.<br /><br /><b>Series Information</b>: Dexter Morgan series<br /><u>Book 1</u>: <i>Darkly Dreaming Dexter</i>, <a href="http://katysozaeva.blogspot.com/2013/08/review-darkly-dreaming-dexter.html" rel="nofollow noopener">review linked here</a><br /><u>Book 2</u>: <i>Dearly Devoted Dexter</i>, <a href="http://katysozaeva.blogspot.com/2013/08/review-dearly-devoted-dexter.html" rel="nofollow noopener">review linked here</a><br /><u>Book 3</u>: <i>Dexter in the Dark</i><br /><u>Book 4</u>: <i>Dexter by Design</i><br /><u>Book 5</u>: <i>Dexter is Delicious</i><br /><u>Book 6</u>: <i>Double Dexter</i><br /><u>Book 7</u>: <i>Dexter's Final Cut</i><br /><br /><b>Disclosure</b>: I purchased this book for myself. All opinions are my own.<br /><br /><b>Synopsis</b>: In his work as a Miami crime scene investigator, Dexter Morgan is accustomed to seeing evil deeds... particularly because, on occasion, he rather enjoys committing them himself. Guided by his Dark Passenger—the voice inside him that helps stalk his prey—he lives his outwardly normal life adhering to one simple rule: he only kills very bad people.<br /><br />Dexter slides through life undetected, working as a blood spatter analyst for the Miami Police Department, helping his fiancee raise her two adorable (if somewhat... unique) children, and always planning his next jaunt as Dexter the Dark Avenger under the light of the full moon.<br /><br />But everything changes when Dexter is called to a gruesome double homicide. Dex realizes he's dealing with someone a whole lot more sinister than he is and it sends the Dark Passenger into hiding. And when something scares your friendly neighborhood serial killer, you know it's serious...<br /><br />More used to inspiring fear then experiencing it, Dex must investigate, while simultaneously coping with is demanding family. If he's to save himself, and those around him, Dexter must pose questions he's never dared ask—where does evil come from, and does it hide inside everyone...?</span>
  <a data-text-id="8017884418338628239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lollie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11110959-lollie"><img alt="Lollie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479165704p2/11110959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/825123466?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lollie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lollie" href="/user/show/11110959-lollie">Lollie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11110959-lollie?shelf=gods-fanatical-religious">gods-fanatical-religious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11110959-lollie?shelf=humourous">humourous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11110959-lollie?shelf=m-for-murder">m-for-murder</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer825123466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13992228795542011470">after reading a few of the other reviews, I think some people may have missed the very subtle point.<br/>In this book Dexter, who is usually so sure of himself, suddenly loses something very close to him. It throws him off. He has no fallback.<br/>People who complained that Dexter wasn't up to his usual witty banter, might do well to think - Who the hell can come up with classic one-liners when you've been off your game for weeks?<br/>This is the whole point, finally seeing Dexter in a vulnerable position.<br/><br/>I fo</span>
  <span id="freeText13992228795542011470" style="display:none">after reading a few of the other reviews, I think some people may have missed the very subtle point.<br />In this book Dexter, who is usually so sure of himself, suddenly loses something very close to him. It throws him off. He has no fallback.<br />People who complained that Dexter wasn't up to his usual witty banter, might do well to think - Who the hell can come up with classic one-liners when you've been off your game for weeks?<br />This is the whole point, finally seeing Dexter in a vulnerable position.<br /><br />I for one am a fan of the writing here. When it comes to first person point of view you won't get gushing verbosity from a man who confesses that he can't feel anything.<br />The simplicity is all part of the design. Too bad that brilliance is wasted on people who want to be spoonfed their books in a conforming mush.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13992228795542011470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128292739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128292739" />
    <a title="Richard Lu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4473894-richard-lu"><img alt="Richard Lu" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128292739?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Lu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Lu" href="/user/show/4473894-richard-lu">Richard Lu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128292739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9944824405432003509">Dexter in the Dark review<br/>	By: Richard Lu<br/><br/>	If you’ve ever seen Dexter on T.V then you’ll probably know that the plot of the show is about a man with dark desires who wishes to kill people. Instead of using these desires to kill innocent people, Dexter only bears his fangs on other predators that have escaped the judgement of the courts. The plot is absolutely gorgeous and it keeps viewers coming back week after week. Thankfully the book version of Dexter has follows the same format, Dexter express</span>
  <span id="freeText9944824405432003509" style="display:none">Dexter in the Dark review<br />	By: Richard Lu<br /><br />	If you’ve ever seen Dexter on T.V then you’ll probably know that the plot of the show is about a man with dark desires who wishes to kill people. Instead of using these desires to kill innocent people, Dexter only bears his fangs on other predators that have escaped the judgement of the courts. The plot is absolutely gorgeous and it keeps viewers coming back week after week. Thankfully the book version of Dexter has follows the same format, Dexter expresses his dark passenger by killing other criminals, just like in the show. If that’s the case than the book “Dexter in the Dark” must be as much of a masterpiece as its television counterpart right? Well no, not really.<br /><br />	Dexter in the Dark is about Dexter losing the voice of the Dark Passenger that drives him to become the murderer that he is. Without it Dexter feels naked and vulnerable to other predators. Dexter then begins his search on why his inner voice left him. While I’ll gladly admit that the first half of the novel was written well enough to keep my interest high, it doesn’t go anywhere but downhill from there. <br /><br />	The second half of Dexter in the Dark is an absolute train wreck, detouring dimensions far away from reality. Apparently the book Dexter’s Dark Passenger is caused by an ancient god named Moloch whom has the ability to multiply itself within the minds of many. These possessed people will then crave blood and become predators. Furthermore, people possessed by Moloch will hear music inside their heads that will put them in trance like states, which I found as being pretty out there. As Desiree had said somewhere below me, the T.V version of Dexter was great because it didn’t feel the need to dive into the origins of the Dark Passenger, keeping the plot feeling realistic.<br /><br />	If you’re like me and you decided to pick up this book because you couldn’t get enough of the television Dexter then do yourself a favour, don’t. Like many of the reviewers below me I found that the addition of the mystical gods crap was both unnecessary and stupid. The Dexter of the book just isn’t the same Dexter that we’ve all come to know and love. Jeff Lindsay’s Dexter in the Dark could have been a great way for fans of Dexter to enjoy more Dexter, as it stands now however, it’s just a big disappointment. Hopefully future Dexter novels will mend the wound inflicted upon Dexter’s good name, though I doubt it, since mystic gods have already been introduced in the world of novel Dex.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9944824405432003509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1077788268" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1077788268" />
    <a title="Siobhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan"><img alt="Siobhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510311895p2/35855553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1077788268?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siobhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siobhan" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan">Siobhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780752881607" href="/book/show/2351235.Dexter_in_the_Dark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1077788268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer23333034343038945">This third book in the Dexter series continues down a route which the television series did not walk upon. As with the second book you will see odds and ends – such as characters and specific acts – which are the same, but as with the second book it is massively different.<br/><br/>This third book allows us to find out a lot more about Dexter’s Dark Passenger. I know that quite a few people disliked the book as it seemed to put an almost supernatural element into the series, yet for me it was my favourite</span>
  <span id="freeText23333034343038945" style="display:none">This third book in the Dexter series continues down a route which the television series did not walk upon. As with the second book you will see odds and ends – such as characters and specific acts – which are the same, but as with the second book it is massively different.<br /><br />This third book allows us to find out a lot more about Dexter’s Dark Passenger. I know that quite a few people disliked the book as it seemed to put an almost supernatural element into the series, yet for me it was my favourite of the books (possibly because I’m a lover of the supernatural). Whilst we found out in the first book what event caused Dexter’s Dark Passenger, in this we find out about the other Dark Passengers which exist in the world – only after Dexter loses his own through the fight or flight response of his Dark Passenger choosing the latter.<br /><br />Whether this almost supernatural twist is loved or hated, the book contains the usual tell-tale Dexter signs. For me, I found there to be more amusing moment than in some of the other books. The ending in particular I found to be highly amusing (but to say anything would be to ruin it for you).<br />If you’re a Dexter fan, even if this twist does put you off, I suggest reading this book. The Dark Passenger details found out in this book do not reappear in later books yet it is nice to get some kind of information.</span>
  <a data-text-id="23333034343038945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">unsophisticated readers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer67686066&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67686066" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1834988167557446084">Have you ever read a book that made you feel like the author was getting between you and the story? There are two authors who have given me this impression: Dean Koontz, and now Jeff Lindsay.<br/><br/>Jeff. Jeff, Jeff, Jeff. You had a good thing going here. The characters were good, the basis of the story was delightfully wicked, and now you've gone and mucked it all up by trying to explain Dexter's motivations and getting all oogie-boogie on us. <br/><br/>I was willing to grit my teeth through your corny and redun</span>
  <span id="freeText1834988167557446084" style="display:none">Have you ever read a book that made you feel like the author was getting between you and the story? There are two authors who have given me this impression: Dean Koontz, and now Jeff Lindsay.<br /><br />Jeff. Jeff, Jeff, Jeff. You had a good thing going here. The characters were good, the basis of the story was delightfully wicked, and now you've gone and mucked it all up by trying to explain Dexter's motivations and getting all oogie-boogie on us. <br /><br />I was willing to grit my teeth through your corny and redundant adjectives for Dexter. I was willing to put up with Deborah (is she that masculine simply because you don't know how to write a woman?). I was cutting you some slack with your portrayal of Rita as a blithering, babbling, annoying woman in spite of the strength she must have to make it through her trials with such grace. But this macabre crap is simply beyond. <br /><br />Stop it, Jeff. Just stop it. Okay?<br /><br />Dexter By Design hits stores in a couple of weeks. I hope it doesn't disappoint. My DP doesn't like authors who disappoint.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3472953754586929508">Well, it started out nice and sick, as any Dexter book should. There's also a very funny exchange that involves the victim of a tongue extraction, the sound "Goy," and the response "Yes. Methodist, actually." Oh, I laughed so hard I was crying.<br/><br/>But then there's a lot of silliness. And, yes, that is the best word for it -- though dumb is challenging it. <br/><br/><b>SPOILER ALERT</b><br/><br/>First of all, Aramaic is written right to left and does not look like the Latin alphbet enough for plebs to decipher it.   <span id="freeText3472953754586929508" style="display:none">Well, it started out nice and sick, as any Dexter book should. There's also a very funny exchange that involves the victim of a tongue extraction, the sound "Goy," and the response "Yes. Methodist, actually." Oh, I laughed so hard I was crying.<br /><br />But then there's a lot of silliness. And, yes, that is the best word for it -- though dumb is challenging it. <br /><br /><b>SPOILER ALERT</b><br /><br />First of all, Aramaic is written right to left and does not look like the Latin alphbet enough for plebs to decipher it. Second, I don't care how rich you are, you can't hynotize people just by playing music alone. Third, there's the issue of Rita's "engagement ring" from <i>Dearly Devoted</i> that is never resolved in that book, and is never addressed here. Ugh. Continuity, people. Please!<br /><br />Still, when you're all doped up on muscle relaxers, this is a good read.</span>

    <a title="Travis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/363023-travis"><img alt="Travis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189406947p2/363023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72199744?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Travis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Travis" href="/user/show/363023-travis">Travis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307276735" href="/book/show/2277439.Dexter_in_the_Dark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/363023-travis?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72199744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer286900911381280352">I also read some of the reviews of <b>Dexter in the Dark</b> before reading and I saw a common theme with most of the reviews; people hated the supernatural aspects. I on the other hand enjoyed the length that the author <i>Jeff Lindsay</i> went through to explain the origins in a very creative and supernatural way that roots human's dark motivations, rituals and religion in this concept of <b>IT</b> or in Dexter's case his <b>Dark Passenger</b>. If there was any gripes about this book was that I was intrigued all the way </span>
  <span id="freeText286900911381280352" style="display:none">I also read some of the reviews of <b>Dexter in the Dark</b> before reading and I saw a common theme with most of the reviews; people hated the supernatural aspects. I on the other hand enjoyed the length that the author <i>Jeff Lindsay</i> went through to explain the origins in a very creative and supernatural way that roots human's dark motivations, rituals and religion in this concept of <b>IT</b> or in Dexter's case his <b>Dark Passenger</b>. If there was any gripes about this book was that I was intrigued all the way through but it didn't hold me in suspense as firmly as the second book did. That may not be <i>Lindsay's</i> fault. I have read two Dexter book prier and I may be burned out a bit. I don't know. I also didn't like aspects of end but hey, every one is an effing critique. This was a solid book and I like it much like the first, I am fond of the second a bit more than both but we all have our favorites. The last two, or so, pages really solidify <i>Lindsay's</i> Dexter as his own and even grow further from the show. The show seems to be growing Dexter with each season while <i>Lindsay</i> places his monster as he is in situations. Dexter may grow but it is a lot slower and not as bold. I really get a kick out of <i>Lindsay's</i> Dexter and can't wait for book four. Actually I may wait. I want to read something else so I can read <b>Dexter by Design</b> with some fresh eyes. Besides enjoying <b>Dexter</b> now catching up to the present books but this is my first series that I will be waiting with anticipation for the next book. I did read <b>Harry Potter</b> but the books were already out by the time I got back to reading them. Thanks sweetheart for picking these books up for me. Love you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="286900911381280352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2983999931993987232" style="display:none">I guess I enjoyed the book. There was a lot missing from it that I thought could have made it more interesting, and while I'm not a big fan of starting an ongoing series in the third book, I made an exception for this since a) the book was free and b) I'd watched the first season of the show. The show itself is really good, and the book is well eh. While I was reading it I didn't dislike it, but now I'm thinking, well there was no police procedural stuff, there was nothing to show that Dexter was any good at his job, and there was really no killing (opps is this a spoiler?) going on (well there was, but off screen kind of stuff). I do know that Dexter likes to eat though, and the amount of times food is mentioned reminds me of the later years of Peanuts and Snoopy's non-sequitar's about wanting a cookie. I think that Charles Shultz was wanting a cookie of his own at the time and someone was telling him he couldn't have one. I don't know if Jeff Lindsay is in the same position, does someone not let him eat? Does he like to eat a little too much? I think I will try maybe reading the first book of the series, and maybe there will be more blood and less food. </span>

<div id="review_157588766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157588766" />
    <a title="Olivia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5197783-olivia"><img alt="Olivia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409358638p2/5197783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157588766?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/5197783-olivia">Olivia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780307455734" href="/book/show/7145902-dexter-in-the-dark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157588766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16260458383746358657">Rather I think 'Lindsay in the Dark'<br/><br/>I must admit that I one of those fans that first experienced Dexter in all its televised glory. And I usually am the one that makes the point of reading the subject to death before watching the movie. And I almost always think that the novel is far superior. My experience with the Dexter novels has been quite the opposite...<br/><br/>After falling in love with our beloved killer on my tv sceen I ran to the library to find the books that inspired such an entrancing tv se</span>
  <span id="freeText16260458383746358657" style="display:none">Rather I think 'Lindsay in the Dark'<br /><br />I must admit that I one of those fans that first experienced Dexter in all its televised glory. And I usually am the one that makes the point of reading the subject to death before watching the movie. And I almost always think that the novel is far superior. My experience with the Dexter novels has been quite the opposite...<br /><br />After falling in love with our beloved killer on my tv sceen I ran to the library to find the books that inspired such an entrancing tv series. Darkly Dreaming Dexter was a major disappointment for me. Simply stating that Dexter was a sociopath that scoffed at the emotional beings living among him every other page ticked me off after the complexities shown on the screen. His complete disregard and even disgust for Rita pissed me off. Simply depicting someone incapable of feeling....incapable of feeling is so expected (hah) if Dexter cares not at all then why should anything matter but himself? Deeper into the novel and I find nothing does.<br /><br />I am aware that this is not a review page for the first novel but it all starts at the roots. After the first novel I decided to disregard their existence and just learn to love the show. Months later I thought to try again and surprisingly loved the Second Novel-Dearly Devoted Dexter. The dry humor kept me laughing into the night.<br /><br />And by the third novel I think I have located my problem with them. Yes Lindsay writes with great humor but without any substance. There is no character development present in any of the novels, nevermind the series as a whole. With a character that claims to be incapable of feeling anything for anyone other than himself development seems an impossibility. Even the teaching of the two children is a lost cause-Dexter thinks constantly about how he must teach them and yet have they learned a thing? No. Other than how to knife a mythical god that has half a sentence's mention in the Bible in the back while your stepdad is grooving out to drums and trumpets with his pants literally on fire. <br /><br />Despite the completely random subject matter that this book is comprised of there are other problems as well. For example Dexter seems pretty stupid throughout the work, and I'm not willing to give all brain cells' credit to the Passenger. And do not get me started on the two page "climax" that closes the work. A whole novel of mind games leads to....an abduction and a dance party? Did it really only take a knife in the back to ruin their whole multi thousand year old plan?<br /><br />In the end the novel was suddenly over and I felt cheated. I read through a hundred pages of that hoping for some explanation and that was it? <br /><br />My advice...first prepare yourself, then maybe read the first novel only and think of it as inspired by the series, and NOT vice versa.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16260458383746358657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vikas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vikas" href="/user/show/3633211-vikas">Vikas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2675449510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10430567792083456867">This was the third book in the series and as usual the TV series was doing its own thing so second onwards it seems that the books will have a different story. So this one was way mysterious and full of hidden dangers<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ but then the final boss or the bad guy turns out to be someone who's shown for the first time and is disposed of fairly quickly and easily like a Kid's play <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.   <span id="freeText10430567792083456867" style="display:none">This was the third book in the series and as usual the TV series was doing its own thing so second onwards it seems that the books will have a different story. So this one was way mysterious and full of hidden dangers<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ but then the final boss or the bad guy turns out to be someone who's shown for the first time and is disposed of fairly quickly and easily like a Kid's play <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Dexter in the Dark was the perfect title though as Dexter had no idea about the plot and then he was also in the dark throughout the book as his Dark Passenger went on a long sabbatical. It had little bit of usual Dexter humour but not much but it seemed true as he would be unhappy if his dark passenger really went on an extended leave without any notice.<br /><br />So yeah pick and read it and probably your experience would be little different or maybe not but no harm in trying, right? and oh yeah after this just Keep on Reading.<br />People who don't read generally ask me my reasons for reading. Simply put I just love reading and so to that end I have made it my motto to just Keep on Reading. I love to read everything except for Self Help books but even those once in a while. I read almost all the genre but YA, Fantasy, Biographies are the most. My favorite series is, of course, Harry Potter but then there are many more books that I just adore. I have bookcases filled with books which are waiting to be read so can't stay and spend more time in this review, so remember I loved reading this and love reading more, you should also read what you love and then just <a href="https://www.keeponreading.in" rel="nofollow noopener">Keep on Reading</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10430567792083456867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QXxofHDK34/CD8Wfz31sIy6aGEqISHkmadcO9wquaOy5Bs5V06n9etmQa90LUMMf4Cxkcljjw4qPC7/FlqVOFQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vuIcLspLG4s+IyGoAZZY+lL8SHoPlVTKWzmCIh2nOTNGmLoHaSg5fiW8j+rFu/fGnEo0Qt8+7ma95TMQgawfyg==')})
  }
